We build it and then we build multiple use cases on top of that

where every use case compounds on, on the one before. So safety is really the entry point for this particular client, but the platform is horizontal, which means we can expand to multiple domains.

So in closing, I'd like to leave you with probably the most important lesson that we've learned so far, and it's as follows.

AI doesn't create durable value through better tools. It creates durable value when you own the intelligence that those tools produce when you on the data, when you own the knowledge, when you own the infrastructure. When you use a vendor's black box AI, the intelligence compounds, but it compounds inside their platform, not yours. When you buy disconnected point solutions, intelligence never compounds because the data behind never connects.

So we feel the best way is a platform first approach where you're able to build something that compounds over time and becomes an organizational asset, not just another tool.

So in 5 years, probably every major AEC firm in the world is going to be running some sort of intelligence layer across their operations. The question that I pose to industry and our clients is whether you want that intelligence to be your asset or somebody else's.

--- SUMMARY ---

Summary

AI in AEC 2026's "Session 11: Construction" showcased the transformative potential of artificial intelligence in the construction industry, featuring six speakers who explored diverse applications of AI, robotics, and hybrid teams. Guido Maciocci introduced ACOS, an AI operating system tailored for architecture, engineering, and construction (AEC) firms, emphasizing its features like connectors, ingestion pipelines, intelligent document processing, knowledge bases, orchestration, automation, and human-in-the-loop review. He highlighted the importance of vendor-neutral platforms that integrate native AEC data to enable compounding intelligence across projects. Roxi Mkhani presented her research on predicting construction errors using AI, leveraging 12 years of data from 20+ business units and 1 million records to develop proactive error classification systems that address inefficiencies caused by rework. Tommy Whitehead showcased his AI tool for automated takeoffs in residential construction, capable of symbol detection, pattern recognition, and automated quantity counts, significantly reducing bottlenecks in estimating processes. Pierpaolo Ruttico demonstrated lightweight bricklaying robots equipped with ergonomic end-effectors and AI vision systems, designed for human-machine collaboration to address labor shortages, improve inclusivity, and reduce musculoskeletal disorders. Karoliina Alatalo explored hybrid human-technology AI teams, presenting a comprehensive roadmap with short-term, medium-term, long-term, and extra-long-term goals for integrating AI and robotics into construction workflows. She also introduced the remote expert concept, utilizing smart glasses to connect site supervisors with remote operators for real-time problem-solving, enhancing efficiency and communication between construction sites and offices. The session highlighted AI's ability to revolutionize construction through collaboration, efficiency, and innovation, paving the way for safer, faster, and higher-quality projects.

is one of the most critical economic sectors for current climate change, accounting for over 39% of global CO2 emissions.

Current construction contains over 28 billion tons of concrete. This is 42% of the global building materials supply.

Cement, which is the basic material of concrete makes up 8% of global CO2 emissions.

28 billion tons of concrete represents a significant source of secondary building parts for reuse, and interdisciplinary team at the Chair of Individualized Production at Arvita Aachen University is developing new methods for material harvesting by increasing the levels of automation in the deconstruction process. The Roboton Research Project bridges this technological gap by transforming an existing manual demolition machine into an automated deconstruction robot. The hardware of the existing Brock de

construct ion machine is extended by attaching motion sensors for each axis. The deconstruction robot is supported by a 2nd mobile robot for environment detection and component recognition.

A digital twin is connected to the robot control through a newly developed user interface. The Roboton Project researches into precise movements of the automated rock joints in Hiltisa. The movements are virtually preplanned, then adapted to construction site requirements.

Concrete is a new source of secondary building material. The aim is to increase the lifetime of existing concrete construction. The Roboton Research Project enables automated deconstruction and the creation of new building processes for modular reuse of harvested concrete building parts. The future of construction is researched at the Reference Construction site of the Center Construction robotics to tackle the shortage of skilled craftsmen. Max is a first automated plug and produce solution to revolutionize scaffold-free facade refurbishment. MAC stands for mobile Assembly X System. Based on the initial patent, an industrial robot works seamlessly with a crane, first tested in a controlled environment. The robot platform

consists of a multi-sensor kua robot for automated assembly of Thunder Max facade panels. Vacuum grippers and the adaptive guiding system allow the controlled lifting of the robot to ensure accurate positioning. Max was then further developed under real conditions and integrated with a mobile Jacko crane. One key innovation is the automated learning of Macs to continue the assembly strategy manually performed by a craftsman.

Max is therefore the first plug and produce system for the future craftsmen being quality controlled via a tablet with no further programming or preplanning skills needed. A second key innovation is that the Jecko crane is controlled by a kuca robot via 5G for safe operation. Max will tackle the skilled labor shortage with speed, safety, and ease to use. Maxwell opened the European refurbishment market of €400 billion to small and

--- SUMMARY ---

Summary

At the "AI in AEC 2026" event's "Closing Session," speakers Sigrid BrellCokcan and Vesa Järvinen delivered an insightful exploration of robotics and AI's transformative role in architecture, engineering, and construction. BrellCokcan traced her journey from early CAD environments and Rhino 1.0 to the adoption of industrial robotics in 2010, catalyzed by the affordability of used robots post-2008. She emphasized the integration of Grasshopper by David Rutten with robotics, enabling novices to simulate processes effectively, and the widespread adoption of Kuka PRC, a robotic platform with over 1.5 million annual downloads.

Innovations like the Robiton research project, which automates deconstruction to harvest materials and reduce concrete's environmental impact, and the MAX system, a scaffold-free facade refurbishment solution that won the Bauma Innovation Award, were highlighted. BrellCokcan advocated for bridging the digital gap between planning and construction sites, emphasizing minimal information modeling and flexible systems to accommodate varying digitalization levels.

Projects such as Kunsthaus Graz and TargetX illustrated the challenges of integrating architectural and structural data, underscoring the need for collaboration across the value chain. Circularity in construction was a key focus, with discussions on controlled deconstruction, material reuse, and the role of cyber-physical systems and edge servers in real-time data processing.

AI's applications in logistics optimization and site supervision were explored, envisioning autonomous night operations where robots manage logistics and documentation. BrellCokcan addressed the challenges posed by hydraulic systems in robotics, emphasizing robust ICT infrastructure and standardized data. Large language models were also discussed for their potential in construction processes.

Regional collaboration gaps in Finland and Norway were noted, with an open invitation for partnerships on European-wide projects. The speakers stressed the importance of community building and communication in advancing construction technology, highlighting AI and robotics' potential to address labor shortages, improve efficiency, and reduce environmental impact. The session concluded with a call for collaboration on future projects, emphasizing the need for systems that adapt to human workflows while fostering innovation.

Speakers

SB

Sigrid BrellCokcan

Director of Individualized Production

RWTH Aachen University

VJ

Vesa Järvinen

AINS Group / A-Insinöörit
